Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Quran for the doctrine that Islam (faith) is created by Allah. The author begins by establishing a linguistic premise about the verb 'ja'ala' (to make), which can be used in two ways: (1) transitive to a single object, meaning to create or bring into existence, and (2) transitive to two objects, meaning to make something described with a certain quality. This premise is supported by Quranic examples. Then the author presents the first proof: the verse 'Our Lord, and make us Muslims for You' (2:128). The argument is that the verb 'ja'ala' here requires Allah to make the believers Muslims, implying that Islam is a direct creation by Allah. An objection is anticipated: the objector points out that 'ja'ala' can have other meanings, such as describing something as something (e.g., calling angels females), giving something the status of something else (e.g., likening believers to the righteous), or enabling/appointing someone to a position (e.g., making someone a leader). The objector asks why the verse cannot be interpreted in one of these ways rather than as creation. The author's initial response is that for the first two meanings (judgment and naming) it is obvious that they do not fit the context. Then a secondary objection is raised: someone might say that this response is invalid for two reasons: (1) every Muslim already deserves to be called Muslim, so there would be no benefit in asking Allah to name them as such; (2) if the meaning were simply naming or describing, then there would be no difference between Allah's 'ja'ala' and any Muslim's description, which is absurd. The author answers the first objection by explaining that being described as Muslim by Allah is the highest honor, akin to asking for a truthful reputation (as in the verse about Abraham). The author answers the second objection by clarifying that Allah's description carries a degree of exaltation that no human description can achieve, analogous to a great king praising someone. The passage thus defends the createdness of Islam through careful linguistic and theological reasoning.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the verse could simply mean 'call us Muslims' as a name, which would not prove creation.
Correction: The author shows that calling or naming would not be the intended meaning because it would be obvious to the objector that those don't fit (hence 'apparent').

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objector suggests that 'make us Muslims' could be just describing or giving status. Have you ever been satisfied with the label of 'Muslim' while your heart was not fully submitted? In what specific area of your life are you just wearing the label without the reality? Will you ask Allah today to actually create submission in you by acting on His command, even if it costs you?
?
The author's reply begins by saying the first two meanings are 'apparent'—meaning it's obvious they don't fit. Is your own submission to Allah so apparent that others see it in your choices? Or are you hiding behind descriptions and status? When you recite this supplication, do you mean for Allah to genuinely transform you, or are you repeating words without expecting change?

Answering the Objection: The Two Reasons and Their Refutation
Author answers two objections against the initial reply: the request is for a unique honor, not a mere label.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two arguments against the author's initial response and how the author refutes them, showing that Allah's naming holds unique honor and distinction.

Core Idea
Allah's description of someone as Muslim is the highest honor, unmatched by any creature's description.

After the author claims that the intended meaning of 'ja'ala' is not judgment/naming, an interlocutor raises a second objection: if 'make us Muslims' meant simply 'call us Muslims,' then (1) it would be pointless since every Muslim already deserves that title, and (2) it would make Allah's act no different from a human's. The author answers both points, arguing that being named Muslim by Allah is the greatest honor, analogous to seeking a truthful reputation, and that divine description carries an incomparable authority.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection
Two reasons are given why the author's initial reply is invalid. Identify them: first, every Muslim is already called Muslim, so asking for it is pointless; second, if it's just naming, then Allah's act is no different from any human's.
2
Examine the first answer
The author answers that being named Muslim by Allah is the highest rank, similar to Abraham asking for a 'tongue of truth' in later generations.
This shows that the request is for divine recognition, not a mere label.
3
Examine the second answer
The author argues that Allah's description carries a degree of exaltation that no human description can match, like a king's praise.
The passage ends mid-sentence but the argument is clear: divine naming is entirely different.

الفصل الثالث في التمسك بالايات المشتملة على لفظ [البصل؟] وما يجي ميره اعلم : أن صيغة جعل ، قد تجيء متعدية إلى مفعول واحد ، ويكون معناها: الإحداث والتكوين. قال تعالى : وجعل الظلمات والنور (۱)) وقد تجيء متعدية إلى مفعولين ويكون معناها : جعل الذات موصوفة بصفة . قال تعالى : وجعلني نبي (٢) ) واجعلنا مسلمين لك (۳) إذا عرفت هذه المقدمة ، فلنذكر الدلائل : الحجة الأولى : قوله تعالى : ( ربنا واجعلنا مسلمين لك (٤) ) وهذا تصريح بأن العبد لا يصير مسلماً ، إلا بأن يجعله الله مسلماً . وذلك يدل على أن الإسلام يحصل بخلق الله . فإن قيل : كما أن الجعل يرد بمعنى التصيير ، فكذلك يرد لوجوه أخرى : أولها : وصف الشيء بالشيء . قال تعالى : ( وجعلوا الملائكة الذين هم عباد الرحمن إناثاً (٥) ) وقال : ( وجعلوا الله شركاء : الجن (1) ) وثانيها : تنزيل الشيء منزلة غيره . قال تعالى : ( أم نجعل الذين آمنوا وعملوا الصالحات ، كالمفسدين في الأرض ، أم نجعل المتقين كالفجار ؟ (۱) ) والتقدير : هل ننزل المصلحين منزلة المفسدين ؟ وكقول القائل إذا نزله منزلة العدو : إنك جعلتني عدوا لنفسك . وثالثها : الإقدار على الشيء ، والتمكين منه . يقال : جعل فلان أميراً وقاضياً . إذا نصب لذلك . قال تعالى : ( إني جاعلك للناس إماماً (٢)) وقال : ( وجعلناهم أئمة (۳)) والمراد منه : النصب لذلك الأمر ، والتعيين له إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد من قوله : ربنا واجعلنا مسلمين لك ) : أحد هذه الوجوه ؟ أما الحكم والتسمية فظاهر ولا يقال : هذا باطل من وجهين : الأول : إن كل مسلم فإنه يستحق أن يسمى مسلماً . فأي فائدة في طلب ذلك من الله تعالى ؟ الثاني : إن المسلمين يصفون المسلمين بالإسلام . وعلى هذا التقدير لا يبقى بين الجعل الصادر من الله تعالى ، وبين الجعل الصادر من كل أحد من أحاد المسلمين فرق لأنا نجيب عن الأول : بأن الإسلام أعظم الخصال الحميدة ، فإذا وصف الله عبداً بذلك ، كان ذلك أشرف المناصب وأعلاها . فلا جرم يحن طلبه من الله تعالى. ونظيره : ما حكى الله في قوله : ( واجعل لي لسان صدق في الآخرين (٤) ) وعن الثاني : إن الله تعالى إذا وصف عبداً بخصلة شريفة ، كان ذلك يوجب من التعظيم والتقديم ما لا يوجبه وصف كل الخلق له بتلك الخصلة . ألا ترى أن الملك العظيم إذا وصف إنساناً ببعض صفات المدح
Chapter three: On adhering to verses containing the word [al-basal?] and what follows. Know that the form 'ja'ala' may come transitive to one object, meaning: innovation and creation. He said Almighty: 'And He made darkness and light.' And it may come transitive to two objects, meaning: making the essence described with a quality. He said Almighty: 'And He made me a prophet' and 'And make us Muslims for You.' If you know this premise, then let us mention the proofs: The first proof: His saying Almighty: 'Our Lord, and make us Muslims for You.' And this is a declaration that the servant does not become Muslim except by Allah making him Muslim. And that indicates that Islam occurs by Allah's creation. For it is said: Just as 'ja'ala' is used in the sense of 'making into,' so also it is used in other ways: First: describing something as something. He said Almighty: 'And they made the angels, who are servants of the Most Merciful, females.' And He said: 'And they made for Allah partners: the jinn.' Second: giving something the status of something else. He said Almighty: 'Or shall We make those who believe and do righteous deeds like the corrupters in the earth, or shall We make the righteous like the wicked?' The interpretation: Do we give the reformers the status of the corrupters? And like the saying of one who gives someone the status of an enemy: 'You have made me an enemy to myself.' Third: enabling someone to do something, and empowering them. It is said: So-and-so was made amir and judge, i.e., appointed to that. He said Almighty: 'Indeed, I will make you a leader for the people' and He said: 'And We made them leaders.' The intent is appointment to that matter and designation for it. If this is established, then we say: Why is it not possible that the intent of His saying 'Our Lord, and make us Muslims for You' is one of these aspects? As for judgment and naming, it is apparent. And it is not said: This is invalid in two ways: First: Every Muslim deserves to be called Muslim. So what benefit is there in asking that from Allah Almighty? Second: The Muslims describe the Muslims with Islam. On this estimation, there remains no distinction between the 'ja'ala' coming from Allah Almighty and the 'ja'ala' coming from any of the common Muslims. For we answer the first: that Islam is the greatest of praiseworthy qualities, so if Allah describes a servant with that, it is the most honorable and highest rank. So naturally it is desired from Allah Almighty. And its analogy is what Allah narrated in His saying: 'And grant me a tongue of truth among the later generations.' And as for the second: that if Allah Almighty describes a servant with a noble quality, that entails a degree of exaltation and precedence that the description of all creatures with that quality does not entail. Do you not see that the great king, if he describes a person with some qualities of praise...
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Quran for the doctrine that Islam (faith) is created by Allah. The author begins by establishing a linguistic premise about the verb 'ja'ala' (to make), which can be used in two ways: (1) transitive to a single object, meaning to create or bring into existence, and (2) transitive to two objects, meaning to make something described with a certain quality. This premise is supported by Quranic examples. Then the author presents the first proof: the verse 'Our Lord, and make us Muslims for You' (2:128). The argument is that the verb 'ja'ala' here requires Allah to make the believers Muslims, implying that Islam is a direct creation by Allah. An objection is anticipated: the objector points out that 'ja'ala' can have other meanings, such as describing something as something (e.g., calling angels females), giving something the status of something else (e.g., likening believers to the righteous), or enabling/appointing someone to a position (e.g., making someone a leader). The objector asks why the verse cannot be interpreted in one of these ways rather than as creation. The author's initial response is that for the first two meanings (judgment and naming) it is obvious that they do not fit the context. Then a secondary objection is raised: someone might say that this response is invalid for two reasons: (1) every Muslim already deserves to be called Muslim, so there would be no benefit in asking Allah to name them as such; (2) if the meaning were simply naming or describing, then there would be no difference between Allah's 'ja'ala' and any Muslim's description, which is absurd. The author answers the first objection by explaining that being described as Muslim by Allah is the highest honor, akin to asking for a truthful reputation (as in the verse about Abraham). The author answers the second objection by clarifying that Allah's description carries a degree of exaltation that no human description can achieve, analogous to a great king praising someone. The passage thus defends the createdness of Islam through careful linguistic and theological reasoning.

Key Terms
حكم
تسمية
فرق
تعظيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that being called Muslim by Allah is just a matter of naming and has no real effect.
Correction: The author shows that it is the greatest honor and carries a special divine status that cannot be achieved by human naming.

Checkpoint
What analogy does the author use to explain why asking Allah to be named Muslim is beneficial?
A) The king's praise
B) The prophet's request for a tongue of truth
C) The angels being called females
D) The believers being likened to the righteous

Key Takeaway
Allah's description of a person as Muslim is the highest honor and entirely distinct from human description, because it stems from divine authority and carries incomparable exaltation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I am a Muslim,' do you genuinely desire that Allah Himself acknowledges you with that title, or is it enough that people around you recognize you as one? What would change in your daily actions if you truly believed that Allah's description of you as Muslim is the highest honor?
?
The author compares the request for being called Muslim to Prophet Ibrahim's plea for a 'tongue of truth' among later generations. Are you living in a way that would make you worthy of such a request? Or do you care more about your reputation among people than your standing with Allah?
?
If you truly internalized that Allah's description of a servant carries an exaltation that no creature's description can match, how would your fear of Allah's displeasure and your hope for His praise transform your relationship with Him tonight?

Scriptural and Rational Proof for the Creation of Actions
Dual proof (scriptural and rational) for creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Aṣbahānī uses both a Qur'anic verse and a rational argument (infinite regress) to establish that all human actions are created by Allah.

Core Idea
The will behind every action must be created by Allah, otherwise an infinite regress would occur.

This lesson presents a concise argument from both scripture and reason for a central Ash'ari doctrine. The author begins with a verse from the Qur'an (Ibrahim 14:40) where Prophet Abraham asks Allah to make him and his offspring establishers of prayer. The argument is that Abraham's request implies that Allah creates the inclination in people's hearts. Then a rational proof is offered: if a person's will were self-generated, it would require an infinite chain of wills. Therefore, all actions are created by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the original Arabic once without analysis, then the literal translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
Notice the verse reference and the logical structure: scriptural then rational.
2
Understand the scriptural inference
The verse shows Prophet Abraham asking Allah to make him and his offspring establishers of prayer. The author infers that this request implies that Allah creates the inclination in people – thus actions are from Allah.
The keyword هنا 'make' indicates creation.
3
Follow the rational argument about will
The argument: If a person's will in the heart were from themselves, it would require another will to will that will, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul). To avoid this, the will must be directly from Allah.
Rational proof uses impossibility of infinite regress.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Both proofs conclude that 'actions of servants are created by Allah.' This is the core Ash'ari position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : ( رب اجعلني مقيم الصلاة ، ومن ذريتي (۱) ) ووجه الاستدلال : أنه أظهر الرغبة إلى الله تعالى في أن يجعل هوى الناس إلى « مكة » . والعقل أيضاً يدل عليه . لأن تحصيل الإرادة في القلب ، إن كان من العبد ، لافتقر فيه إلى إرادة أخرى ، ولزم التسلسل . وإن كان من الله تعالى فهو المطلوب . وكل ذلك تصريح بأن أفعال العباد مخلوقة الله سبحانه .
And His saying: 'My Lord, make me an establisher of prayer, and from my offspring [as well]' (1). And the face of the inference is that he manifested desire to Allah Most High that He make the inclination of people towards 'Mecca'. And the intellect also indicates it. Because the acquisition of will (irada) in the heart, if it is from the servant, would require another will, and infinite regress (tasalsul) would follow. And if it is from Allah Most High, then that is what is sought. And all of that is a declaration that the actions of servants are created by Allah, exalted is He.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents a dual proof—scriptural and rational—for the Ash'ari doctrine that human actions are created by Allah. The author begins with a verse: Prophet Abraham's prayer 'My Lord, make me an establisher of prayer...' The argument is that Abraham asked Allah to make people's inclination toward Mecca, implying that Allah creates that inclination. Then the author adds a rational proof: If a person's will (irada) were self-generated, it would require a prior will to will that will, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul). To avoid this, the will must be created directly by Allah. The conclusion: 'all that is a declaration that the actions of servants are created by Allah.' This is a classic kalam argument against free will (qadar).

Key Terms

تسلسل
أفعال العباد مخلوقة لله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans independently create their own actions and will.
Correction: The passage argues that if will were self-generated, infinite regress would follow; thus will must be created by Allah.

Checkpoint
What is the rational argument used in this passage?
A) Creation of actions is known by consensus.
B) If the will came from the servant, infinite regress would follow.
C) Actions are caused by atoms.
D) The verse proves predestination.

Key Takeaway
Both scripture and reason converge on the conclusion that all human actions are created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you ever feel proud as if it originated from you alone? How does realizing that even your will to pray is created by Allah humble you? This week, before each prayer, silently acknowledge 'Allah created my desire to pray' and see how it changes your heart.
?
Have you ever used 'I don't have the willpower' as an excuse to avoid good? This lesson teaches that even your lack of will is not independent of Allah. What would it mean for you to urgently beg Him, like Ibrahim, 'My Lord, make me an establisher of prayer'? Write down one area where you feel weak and turn it into a specific du'a today.
?
The rational proof shows that an infinite regress of wills is absurd. In your daily life, do you act as though your choices are self-caused, forgetting the Creator? How can you re-train your mind to see Allah's creation in every decision? Commit to saying 'La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah' at least five times today when you feel self-sufficient.

Contextual Proof: The Verse 'Wa-j'alhu Rabbi Radhiyyan'
Author defends a scriptural proof using context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the context of the verse 'Wa-j'alhu Rabbi Radhiyyan' proves that Allah creates religious merit, not just physical attributes.

Core Idea
Context determines meaning: a prophet's request for religious perfection confirms creation of religious actions.

In this passage, the author defends a scriptural proof for the creation of actions by addressing an objection. The opponent claims that the word 'pleasing' in the verse could refer to physical perfection, which is also from Allah. The author uses the surrounding context—specifically the mention of inheritance of religion—to show that the verse refers to religious pleasingness, thereby reinforcing the doctrine that Allah creates all human actions, including religious merit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objection
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that an objection is raised: 'radiyyan' might mean physical perfection. The author then provides an answer.
The objection is based on the possibility of a different interpretation.
2
Understand the author's argument about context
The author argues that the preceding verse mentions inheritance of religion and prophethood. This context determines that 'radiyyan' must refer to religious pleasingness.
The principle is that an ambiguous word (mujmal) should be interpreted by its immediate context.
3
Examine the two pieces of evidence
The author gives two reasons why the inheritance is religious: (1) majority of commentators say so, (2) a prophet's concern is primarily for religious interests.
These strengthen the contextual argument.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
If 'radiyyan' means religious approval, then the verse shows that Allah creates religious merit in the servant, supporting the creation of actions.
This connects to the broader topic of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : قوله تعالى : ( واجعله رب رضيا (۲) ) فإن قيل : عليه الأسئلة التي (۳) تقدم ذكرها في الحجة الأولى . فالذي نزيده ههنا أن نقول : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد كونه رضيا في الخلقة والصورة . وهو كونه تام الخلقة ، الحواس ، كامل العقل ، شديد القوة ، طلق الوجه ، حسن الصورة ، موصوفاً بالأخلاق الحميدة ، محبوباً بين الناس ؟ وكل ذلك من أفعال الله تعالى . والجواب : إن مقدمة الآية هي قوله : ( يرثني ، ويرث من آل يعقوب (٤) ) : وهذه الوراثة هي وراثة الدين والنبوة ، لا وراثة المال . ويدل عليه وجهان : الأول : إن جمهور المفسرين قالوا بذلك . والثاني : إن عمل مبالغة الرسول المعصوم وهو زكريا عليه السلام على حفظ مصالح الدين ، أولى من عمله على حفظ مصالح الدنيا ، فثبت : أن المراد من قوله يرثني ويرث من آل يعقوب وراثة الدين والنبوة. ثم إنه تعالى قال بعده : ( واجعله رب رضياً ) فوجب أن يكون مراده منه : كونه رضياً في الدين . لأن حمل اللفظ المجمل على المذكور السابق ، أولى من حمله على الشيء الأجنبي .
The fourth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And make him, my Lord, pleasing (radiyyan)' (2). For if it is said: upon it are the questions that were mentioned in the first proof. Then what we add here is to say: why may it not be permissible that what is meant is his being pleasing in constitution and form—that is, his being perfect in constitution, senses, complete in intellect, strong in power, cheerful of face, beautiful of form, described with praiseworthy morals, beloved among people? And all of that is from the actions of Allah Most High. The answer: Indeed the premise of the verse is His saying: 'He will inherit from me and inherit from the house of Jacob' (4). And this inheritance is the inheritance of religion and prophethood, not the inheritance of wealth. And two aspects indicate this: First, that the majority of commentators said that. Second, that the action of one who is concerned, the infallible messenger Zechariah, peace be upon him, is more fitting for preserving the interests of religion than for preserving worldly interests. So it is established that what is meant by his saying 'he will inherit from me and inherit from the house of Jacob' is the inheritance of religion and prophethood. Then He, exalted, said after it: 'And make him, my Lord, pleasing.' So it is necessary that what is meant by it is his being pleasing in religion, because carrying the ambiguous word (al-mujmal) upon what was mentioned previously is more appropriate than carrying it upon something extraneous.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth scriptural proof for the creation of actions, structured as an objection and answer. The author cites the verse 'And make him, my Lord, pleasing' (19:6). The objection suggests that 'pleasing' could mean physically perfect—complete in form, senses, intellect, strength, etc.—all of which are indeed from Allah, so the verse would still support creation of actions. The author answers by focusing on the immediate context: the preceding verse speaks of inheritance—'He will inherit from me and inherit from the house of Jacob.' The author argues that this inheritance is religious and prophetic, not material, based on two reasons: first, the majority of commentators interpret it that way; second, the concern of a prophet like Zechariah is primarily for religious interests, not worldly ones. Therefore, since the context establishes religious inheritance, the following request 'make him pleasing' must also refer to religious pleasingness (being pleasing in religion). The principle invoked is that when a word is ambiguous (mujmal), it should be interpreted in light of the preceding context rather than something extraneous. This refutes the objection and reinforces that the verse proves Allah creates religious merit in servants.

Key Terms
رضيا (radiyyan)
وراثة الدين والنبوة (wirathat al-din wa al-nubuwwa)
المجمل (al-mujmal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Wa-j'alhu Rabbi Radhiyyan' refers only to physical perfection.
Correction: The preceding context of religious inheritance shows it refers to religious pleasingness, not physical attributes.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the interpretation that 'radiyyan' refers to physical perfection?
A) Because the preceding verse mentions inheritance of religion and prophethood.
B) Because Allah only creates religious attributes.
C) Because physical perfection is not a blessing.
D) Because the author prefers a metaphorical reading.

Key Takeaway
The context of a verse is essential for correct interpretation; here it proves Allah creates religious merit in His servants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse of the Quran, do you first check its context before forming an opinion? How often do you let your own assumptions override the surrounding message? Commit today to reading at least the five verses before and after any verse you quote.
?

?
The author argues that being 'pleasing' to Allah (radiyyan) is about religious virtue, not outward appearance or worldly success. If you were to evaluate your own life by that standard alone, would you be pleased with what you see? What is one religious quality you lack that you will ask Allah sincerely to grant you, starting today?

The Fifth Proof: Mercy and Affection Placed by Allah
Author cites two verses to prove that Allah creates acts of obedience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses verses about mercy and affection to prove that all acts of obedience are created by Allah.

Core Idea
Allah directly places mercy in hearts, so acts of obedience come from Him.

The author continues his series of proofs for the creation of human actions by turning to the Quran. He selects two verses that explicitly state that Allah places mercy, compassion, and affection in people's hearts. Since these qualities are clearly acts of obedience (ta'at), and Allah is the one who places them, the conclusion is that all acts of obedience are created by Allah. This lesson will walk through this simple but powerful scriptural argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the structure: the proof is introduced, then two verses are cited, and a conclusion is drawn.
2
Identify the two verses
Identify the two Quranic verses cited. One mentions 'ra'fa and rahma' (compassion and mercy) in the hearts of the followers of Prophet Jesus, and the other mentions 'mawadda and rahma' (affection and mercy) between spouses.
3
Understand the key point
The author asserts that these qualities are 'among the great acts of obedience.' Why does he consider them acts of obedience? Because they are righteous qualities commanded by Allah.
4
Follow the logical conclusion
Since Allah Himself explicitly states that He 'placed' these acts of obedience in hearts, then He is the creator of those acts. Therefore, all acts of obedience are created by Allah.
This is a direct quranic proof for the creation of human actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى : ( وجعلنا في قلوب الذين اتبعوه : رأفة ورحمة (۱) ) ويقرب منه : قوله تعالى : ( وجعل بينكم مودة ورحمة (۲) ) ولا شك أن تلك المودة والرحمة من الطاعات العظيمة. فدل ذلك : على أن طاعات العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى .
The fifth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy' (1). And close to it is His saying, exalted: 'And He placed between you affection and mercy' (2). And there is no doubt that that affection and mercy are among the great acts of obedience (ta'at). So that indicates that the acts of obedience of the servants are created by Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents a concise scriptural proof for the creation of human actions. The author cites two verses where Allah explicitly states that He 'placed' (ja'ala) compassion, mercy, and affection in hearts. These qualities are described as 'among the great acts of obedience' (ta'at). Since these are acts of obedience, and Allah Himself places them, it follows that the acts of obedience of servants are created by Allah. The argument is straightforward: if Allah creates these good qualities, and they are acts of obedience, then all acts of obedience are created by Allah. No objection is raised here; the proof is presented as self-evident.

Key Terms
رأفة (ra'fa)
رحمة (rahma)
مودة (mawadda)
طاعات (ta'at)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that mercy and affection are simply natural human traits that arise spontaneously, not created by Allah.
Correction: The verses clearly state that Allah 'placed' these qualities, indicating they are created and given by Allah. Moreover, the author classifies them as acts of obedience, which are also created.

Checkpoint

A) That believers have mercy.
B) That acts of obedience are created by Allah.
C) That marriage is a source of mercy.
D) That Allah loves mercy.

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof uses Quranic statements to show that Allah Himself claims to place mercy and affection in hearts, establishing that acts of obedience are created by Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel genuine mercy or affection for someone, do you credit yourself or recognize that Allah placed it in your heart? What changes if you truly believe that even your best emotions are created by Him?
?
If your acts of obedience—including the love you feel for others—are directly created by Allah, does that humble you or make you more grateful? How will you remind yourself of this truth before your next good deed?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and knowing that every ounce of mercy you showed was His gift. Does that make you more careful to act on those feelings, knowing they are not mere accidents but divine placements? What specific step will you take today to act on a mercy Allah has placed in your heart?

The Sixth Proof: Enemies of Prophets
Author presents proof and addresses objection that 'ja'ala' means 'judged'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof regarding enemies of prophets and the objection concerning the meaning of 'ja'ala', along with the beginning of the response.

Core Idea
'Ja'ala' in the Qur'an means creation, not mere judgment.

This passage presents the sixth proof that Allah creates the enemies of prophets, citing key verses. An objection is raised that 'ja'ala' might mean 'judged' rather than 'created'. The author begins to answer by first appealing to the natural causation of envy and then directly addressing the linguistic interpretation. We will examine the proof, the objection, and the initial steps of the reply.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof verses
The author quotes two verses where Allah says He 'made' enemies for every prophet. Read them carefully.
Notice the wording 'ja'alna' (We made).
2
Understand the objection
The objection suggests that 'ja'ala' might mean 'judged' or 'named', not 'created'. This would weaken the proof. What does the author say in response?
The response has two parts: first a causal argument, then a direct linguistic answer.
3
Examine the beginning of the answer
The author starts by saying that the interpretation of 'ja'ala' as judgment is against the apparent meaning. Then he begins another point that is cut off. Consider why he insists on the literal meaning.
The answer is incomplete in this passage.

الحجة السادسة : قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي : عدوا من المجرمين (۳) ) ونظيره قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي : عدوا . شياطين الإنس والجن (٤) ) فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد منه : الحكم بكون أولئك المجرمين ، أعداء لذلك النبي ؟ فنقول : المراد : أنه تعالى لما خصص الرسل بالكرامات الفائقة ، والفضائل العظيمة ، التي بسببها يحسدهم الكفار ، ويعادونهم ، صار كأنه تعالى هو الذي جعلهم أعداء لأولئك الأنبياء ، وإليه أشار المتنبي بقوله : أزل حسد الحساد عني بكبتهم فأنت الذي صيرتهم لي حسداً . ثم الذي يدل على أنه لا بد من المصير إلى هذه التأويلات : جميع الآيات الدالة على أنه تعالى ينصر الأنبياء والرسل . قال - تعالى - : ( هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى، ودين الحق ؛ ليظهره على الدين كله . ولو كره المشركون (٥) ) وقال : ( وينصرك الله نصراً عزيزاً(1) ) فكيف يليق بمثل هذا الإعزاز ، أن يلقى عداوته في قلوب الناس ؟ والجواب : أما تفسير لفظ الجعل بالحكم والتسمية . فقد ذكرنا أنه خلاف الظاهر . وأيضاً : لو سلمنا ذلك . إلا أن الله تعالى لما كان قد حكم به
The sixth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals' (3). And its parallel: His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy—devils of mankind and jinn' (4). For if it is said: Why may it not be permissible that what is meant by it is the judgment that those criminals are enemies of that prophet? We say: the meaning is that He, exalted, when He distinguished the messengers with superior honors and great virtues, due to which the disbelievers envy them and oppose them, it became as if He, exalted, is the one who made them enemies of those prophets. And to this al-Mutanabbi alluded with his saying: 'Remove the envy of the envious from me by suppressing them, for You are the one who made them envious of me.' Then what indicates that it is necessary to resort to these interpretations is all the verses indicating that He, exalted, supports the prophets and messengers. He, exalted, said: 'He is the one who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it' (5). And He said: 'And Allah will support you with a mighty victory' (1). So how is it fitting for such glorification that He should cast enmity into the hearts of people? The answer: As for the interpretation of the word 'making' (ja'ala) as judgment and naming, we have mentioned that it is contrary to the apparent meaning. And also: Even if we accept that, Allah Most High, since He judged by it...
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof, which cites verses where Allah says He 'made' enemies for every prophet. The objection is that 'made' (ja'ala) might mean 'judged' (hukm) or 'named' (tasmiya), not 'created'—i.e., Allah merely declared them enemies, not created their enmity. The author's initial response (prior to the formal 'jawab') argues that since Allah gave prophets superior honors that naturally cause envy, He is effectively the cause of their enmity, as the poet al-Mutanabbi expressed. Then the author adds a supplementary argument: verses showing that Allah supports and glorifies prophets contradict the idea that He would create enmity in people's hearts against them—so the only way to reconcile is to interpret the 'making' as indirect causation. Then comes the formal 'jawab' (answer), which begins by rejecting the interpretation of 'ja'ala' as judgment/naming, calling it contrary to the apparent meaning (khilaf al-zahir). Then it starts another point ('Also: even if we accept that...') which is cut off. The answer is incomplete, but the direction is clear: the author maintains that the apparent meaning of 'ja'ala' is creation, and the reinterpretation is not acceptable. This passage illustrates the Ash'ari insistence on the literal, creative sense of 'ja'ala' in such verses.

Key Terms
جعل (ja'ala)
حكم (hukm)
تسمية (tasmiya)
عدو (aduw)
تأويل (ta'wil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'ja'ala' in these verses means 'judged' or 'named' and does not indicate creation.
Correction: The apparent meaning and context show that 'ja'ala' here refers to Allah making enemies as a creation, either directly or indirectly.

Checkpoint
What is the objection raised against this proof?
A) The verse is abrogated.
B) The word 'ja'ala' might mean 'judged' not 'created'.
C) The enemies were not real.
D) The prophets created their own enemies.

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof uses verses about enemies to show Allah's creation, and the objection that 'ja'ala' means 'judged' is rejected because it contradicts apparent meaning and other verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author uses al-Mutanabbi's line: 'You are the one who made them envious of me.' When someone opposes you because of your faith or character, do you see that as Allah's doing? How does that change your reaction toward that person?
?
If 'ja'ala' in the Qur'an always means creation, then your own enmity toward truth—past or present—is something Allah created. Will you now ask Him to re-create your heart into one that loves what He loves, even if it requires admitting you were wrong?

Fifth Proof: Verses on Affection and Mercy
The fifth proof argues that affections and mercies are acts of obedience created by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verses about affection and mercy serve as evidence that acts of obedience are created by Allah.

Core Idea
Affection and mercy in hearts are acts of obedience created by Allah.

This lesson introduces the fifth proof in the series of evidences for the creation of human actions. The author cites two Quranic verses that explicitly attribute affection and mercy to Allah's act of placing (ja'l). After establishing that these affections are great acts of obedience, the conclusion follows that such acts are created by Allah. This proof reinforces the broader theological position that all human actions, including obedient ones, are under divine creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own flow come through.
Notice the structure: two verse citations followed by a conclusion.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Look at the first verse about 'those who followed him' and the second about between spouses. Note what Allah placed (ja'l) in each case.
The first verse is from Surah Al-Hadid, the second from Surah Ar-Rum.
3
Understand the inference
The author states that these affections are among the great acts of obedience. Therefore, because Allah placed them, they are created by Him. This is the core argument.
Think: if Allah makes something, that thing is a created object.
4
Consider the larger implication
This proof supports the doctrine that all human actions, including acts of obedience, are created by Allah. Reflect on why this matters for the kalam topic of qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى : ( وجعلنا في قلوب الذين اتبعوه : رأفة ورحمة (۱) ) ويقرب منه : قوله تعالى : ( وجعل بينكم مودة ورحمة (۲) ) ولا شك أن تلك المودة والرحمة من الطاعات العظيمة. فدل ذلك : على أن طاعات العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى .
The fifth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy (1)' and close to it is His saying, exalted: 'And He placed between you affection and mercy (2)'. There is no doubt that that affection and mercy are among the great acts of obedience. So that indicates that the acts of obedience of the servants are created by Allah, exalted.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof for the creation of human actions, specifically acts of obedience. The author cites two Quranic verses: one stating that Allah placed compassion and mercy in the hearts of followers of prophets, and another stating that He placed affection and mercy between spouses. The author argues that these affections and mercies are themselves acts of obedience—great ones. Since they are explicitly attributed to Allah's act of making (ja'l), it follows that these obedient acts are created by Allah. The underlying logic is: whatever is directly created by Allah in human hearts is an act of obedience, and that act is therefore a created thing. This supports the doctrine that all human actions, including obedient ones, are created by Allah.

Misconception: One might think that attributing affection to Allah's making means only the feeling is created, not the act itself.
Correction: The author explicitly states that these affections are among the great acts of obedience, so both the feeling and the obedient act are created by Allah.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If every good inclination—even your desire to be kind—is directly created by Allah, then what room is left for pride in your own goodness? Examine your heart: do you secretly believe your kindness originates from you? Confess that to Allah and ask Him to create in you pure obedience, both inward and outward.
?
The proof shows that Allah places mercy and affection as acts of obedience. Are you actively seeking from Allah the creation of these inner states, or do you rely solely on your own efforts? This week, make a specific du'a for Allah to place mercy in your heart toward someone you find difficult to love.

The Sixth Proof and the Initial Objection
The author presents the sixth proof from the Quran and raises an objection about the interpretation of 'ja'l'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof based on the verse about Allah making enemies for prophets, and the initial objection that the word 'ja'l' might mean judgment rather than creation.

Core Idea
Allah's making of enemies is real, not merely judgmental.

This lesson introduces the sixth proof from the Quranic verse that Allah 'made' enemies for every prophet. We will examine the apparent meaning and an early objection that tries to reinterpret the word 'ja'l' as a judgment. This sets up the theological debate about divine causation of human actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its parallel
Read the two Quranic verses that state Allah made enemies for prophets. Notice the clear wording 'ja'alna' (We made).
2
Understand the apparent meaning
The apparent meaning is that Allah directly creates enmity. Reflect on why this might be problematic for some theological positions.
This is the basis of the sixth proof.
3
Consider the objection
The objection suggests that 'ja'l' might mean 'judgment' (hukm) rather than creation. Think about how this reinterpretation would affect the proof.
The author will respond in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي : عدوا من المجرمين (۳) ) ونظيره قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي : عدوا . شياطين الإنس والجن (٤) )
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد منه : الحكم بكون أولئك المجرمين ، أعداء لذلك النبي ؟ فنقول : المراد : أنه تعالى لما خصص الرسل بالكرامات الفائقة ، والفضائل العظيمة ، التي بسببها يحسدهم الكفار ، ويعادونهم ، صار كأنه تعالى هو الذي جعلهم أعداء لأولئك الأنبياء ، وإليه أشار المتنبي بقوله : أزل حسد الحساد عني بكبتهم فأنت الذي صيرتهم لي حسداً
ثم الذي يدل على أنه لا بد من المصير إلى هذه التأويلات : جميع الآيات الدالة على أنه تعالى ينصر الأنبياء والرسل . قال - تعالى - : ( هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى، ودين الحق ؛ ليظهره على الدين كله . ولو كره المشركون (٥) ) وقال : ( وينصرك الله نصراً عزيزاً(1) ) فكيف يليق بمثل هذا الإعزاز ، أن يلقى عداوته في قلوب الناس ؟
والجواب : أما تفسير لفظ الجعل بالحكم والتسمية . فقد ذكرنا أنه خلاف الظاهر . وأيضاً : لو سلمنا ذلك . إلا أن الله تعالى لما كان قد حكم به في اللوح المحفوظ، كان حصوله واجباً ، وتركه ممتنعاً . لما بينا أن تركه يقتضي انقلاب خبر الله ، الصدق : كذباً . وإنه محال . وأما الذي ذكروه في الوجه الثاني فضعيف جداً . وذلك لأن تخصيص الرسل بتلك الكرامات وتلك الفضائل لا يوجب حصول العداوة . ألا ترى أن تلك الفضائل هي التي صارت أسباباً قوية الحصول المحبة الشديدة في قلوب الأولياء . ولو كان حصول تلك الفضائل ، موجباً لحصول العداوة ، لكان السبب الواحد موجباً حصول ضدين . وهو محال . بل الحق : أن ذلك لا يوجب ، لا حصول المحبة ، ولا حصول العداوة . وأن الموجب لحصول المحبة : إلقاء دواعي المحبة في القلوب ، والموجب لحصول العداوة : إلقاء دواعي العداوة في القلوب . وعلى هذا التقدير يكون الكل من الله . وعند استحضار مسألة الداعي على الوجه الذي لخصناه ، يظهر أن ظاهر قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي عدوا من المجرمين ) متأكداً هذا البرهان العقلي القاطع ، الذي لا يقدر أحد على التشكيك فيه بوجه من الوجوه . وبالله التوفيق .
The sixth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals (3)' and its parallel is His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy: devils of mankind and jinn (4)'. If it is said: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by it is the judgment that those criminals are enemies of that prophet? Then we say: The meaning is that when He, exalted, distinguished the messengers with surpassing honors and great virtues, because of which the disbelievers envy them and oppose them, it is as if He, exalted, is the one who made them enemies of those prophets. And al-Mutanabbi alluded to this with his saying: 'Remove the envy of the envious from me by repressing them, for You are the one who made them envious of me.' Then what indicates that it is necessary to resort to these interpretations is all the verses indicating that He, exalted, supports the prophets and messengers. He, exalted, said: 'He is the one who sent His messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it (5)' and He said: 'And Allah will support you with a mighty victory (6).' So how is it befitting such honor that enmity towards him be cast into the hearts of people? And the answer: As for the interpretation of the word 'ja'l' as 'judgment and naming', we have mentioned that it is contrary to the apparent meaning. Also, even if we grant that, yet when Allah, exalted, had judged it in the Preserved Tablet, its occurrence was necessary and its omission impossible. Because we have shown that its omission would necessitate the turning of Allah's truthful news into falsehood, which is impossible. And as for what they mentioned in the second point, it is very weak. This is because distinguishing the messengers with those honors and those virtues does not necessitate the occurrence of enmity. Do you not see that those virtues are what became strong causes for the occurrence of intense love in the hearts of the saints? And if the occurrence of those virtues necessitated the occurrence of enmity, then one cause would necessitate the occurrence of two opposites, which is impossible. Rather, the truth is that that does not necessitate either the occurrence of love or the occurrence of enmity. And that which necessitates the occurrence of love is the casting of motives of love into hearts, and that which necessitates the occurrence of enmity is the casting of motives of enmity into hearts. On this basis, everything is from Allah. And when the issue of the motive (al-da'i) is recalled in the manner we summarized, it becomes apparent that the apparent meaning of His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals' is confirmed by this decisive rational proof, which no one is able to cast doubt upon in any way. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof and contains a lengthy dialectic. The author first cites two verses that explicitly say 'We made for every prophet an enemy.' The apparent meaning is that Allah creates enmity. Then an objection is raised: could the word 'ja'l' here mean 'judgment' (i.e., Allah merely judges them to be enemies) rather than creating? The author gives a preliminary response: the virtues bestowed on prophets naturally cause envy, so it is as if Allah made them enemies. Then the author provides supporting evidence from verses showing Allah supports prophets, implying He would not cast enmity into hearts—so the interpretation as judgment is needed. But then the author delivers the final answer: first, interpreting 'ja'l' as judgment is against the apparent meaning. Second, even if we accept that interpretation, if Allah's judgment is in the Preserved Tablet, then the occurrence of enmity becomes necessary (since Allah's news is true), so it still amounts to creation of enmity by necessity. Third, the alternative explanation that the virtues themselves cause enmity is weak because the same virtues cause love in saints, and one cause cannot produce two opposites. The true cause of enmity is the casting of motives into hearts, which is from Allah. Thus all is from Allah, and the verse is confirmed by rational proof. This is a classic kalam argument for the creation of all actions, even those of enemies.

Key Terms
الجعل
العداوة
الحكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'ja'l' can always be interpreted metaphorically as judgment, thereby denying that Allah directly creates actions.
Correction: The author shows that the apparent meaning is creation, and even the metaphorical interpretation leads to the same conclusion when combined with the Preserved Tablet argument.

Checkpoint
What is the initial objection raised against the apparent meaning of the verse?
A) The verse is not authentic.
B) The word 'ja'l' might mean 'judgment' rather than 'creation'.
C) The verse applies only to prophets before Prophet Muhammad.
D) The enemies were not real.

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof relies on the apparent meaning that Allah creates enemies, with an early objection reinterpreting 'ja'l' as judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone opposes you because of your commitment to Islam, do you see that as random hostility, or do you recognize Allah's hand in making that person an adversary as part of your test? Will you treat them with the same patience the prophets showed?
?
The lesson says Allah's bestowal of honors upon the prophets triggered envy and opposition. In your own life, when you are granted a blessing—knowledge, good character, or status—does envy from others surprise you? How does knowing that this can be from Allah change how you respond to their resentment?
?
If Allah 'makes' enemies for those He loves, are you willing to accept that the opposition you face might be a sign of divine favor rather than misfortune? What would it mean for you to embrace that truth and entrust the outcome to Him?

The Answer and the Rational Proof
The author provides a detailed answer to the objection and a rational proof that Allah creates enmity by casting motives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's comprehensive refutation of the objection and the rational proof that confirms Allah's creation of enmity through casting motives into hearts.

Core Idea
Allah creates enmity by casting motives, not through virtues alone.

This lesson presents the author's final answer to the objection. He argues that even if 'ja'l' meant judgment, it would still necessitate enmity because Allah's decree in the Preserved Tablet is unchangeable. He also refutes the idea that the virtues of prophets directly cause enmity, showing that the same virtues cause love in saints, so one cause cannot produce two opposites. The true cause is Allah's casting of motives into hearts.

Guided Path
1
Examine the counter-evidence
Read the supporting verses that show Allah supports prophets. Consider why this implies He would not create enmity unless it were consistent with His plan.
2
Understand the answer about 'ja'l'
The author first states that interpreting 'ja'l' as judgment is against the apparent meaning. Then he shows that even if accepted, Allah's judgment in the Preserved Tablet makes the enmity necessary.
This turns the objection back on itself.
3
Refute the virtues argument
The author argues that the same virtues that cause love in saints cannot logically cause enmity in disbelievers, as one cause cannot produce two opposites.
4
Learn the true cause
The author explains that the cause of love or enmity is Allah's casting of motives (ad'iyah) into hearts. Thus, everything is from Allah.
This confirms the verse's apparent meaning with a rational proof.

فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد منه : الحكم بكون أولئك المجرمين ، أعداء لذلك النبي ؟ فنقول : المراد : أنه تعالى لما خصص الرسل بالكرامات الفائقة ، والفضائل العظيمة ، التي بسببها يحسدهم الكفار ، ويعادونهم ، صار كأنه تعالى هو الذي جعلهم أعداء لأولئك الأنبياء ، وإليه أشار المتنبي بقوله : أزل حسد الحساد عني بكبتهم فأنت الذي صيرتهم لي حسداً
ثم الذي يدل على أنه لا بد من المصير إلى هذه التأويلات : جميع الآيات الدالة على أنه تعالى ينصر الأنبياء والرسل . قال - تعالى - : ( هو الذي أرسل رسوله بالهدى، ودين الحق ؛ ليظهره على الدين كله . ولو كره المشركون (٥) ) وقال : ( وينصرك الله نصراً عزيزاً(1) ) فكيف يليق بمثل هذا الإعزاز ، أن يلقى عداوته في قلوب الناس ؟
والجواب : أما تفسير لفظ الجعل بالحكم والتسمية . فقد ذكرنا أنه خلاف الظاهر . وأيضاً : لو سلمنا ذلك . إلا أن الله تعالى لما كان قد حكم به في اللوح المحفوظ، كان حصوله واجباً ، وتركه ممتنعاً . لما بينا أن تركه يقتضي انقلاب خبر الله ، الصدق : كذباً . وإنه محال . وأما الذي ذكروه في الوجه الثاني فضعيف جداً . وذلك لأن تخصيص الرسل بتلك الكرامات وتلك الفضائل لا يوجب حصول العداوة . ألا ترى أن تلك الفضائل هي التي صارت أسباباً قوية الحصول المحبة الشديدة في قلوب الأولياء . ولو كان حصول تلك الفضائل ، موجباً لحصول العداوة ، لكان السبب الواحد موجباً حصول ضدين . وهو محال . بل الحق : أن ذلك لا يوجب ، لا حصول المحبة ، ولا حصول العداوة . وأن الموجب لحصول المحبة : إلقاء دواعي المحبة في القلوب ، والموجب لحصول العداوة : إلقاء دواعي العداوة في القلوب . وعلى هذا التقدير يكون الكل من الله . وعند استحضار مسألة الداعي على الوجه الذي لخصناه ، يظهر أن ظاهر قوله تعالى : ( وكذلك جعلنا لكل نبي عدوا من المجرمين ) متأكداً هذا البرهان العقلي القاطع ، الذي لا يقدر أحد على التشكيك فيه بوجه من الوجوه . وبالله التوفيق .
The sixth proof: His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals (3)' and its parallel is His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy: devils of mankind and jinn (4)'. If it is said: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by it is the judgment that those criminals are enemies of that prophet? Then we say: The meaning is that when He, exalted, distinguished the messengers with surpassing honors and great virtues, because of which the disbelievers envy them and oppose them, it is as if He, exalted, is the one who made them enemies of those prophets. And al-Mutanabbi alluded to this with his saying: 'Remove the envy of the envious from me by repressing them, for You are the one who made them envious of me.' Then what indicates that it is necessary to resort to these interpretations is all the verses indicating that He, exalted, supports the prophets and messengers. He, exalted, said: 'He is the one who sent His messenger with guidance and the religion of truth to make it prevail over all religion, even if the polytheists dislike it (5)' and He said: 'And Allah will support you with a mighty victory (6).' So how is it befitting such honor that enmity towards him be cast into the hearts of people? And the answer: As for the interpretation of the word 'ja'l' as 'judgment and naming', we have mentioned that it is contrary to the apparent meaning. Also, even if we grant that, yet when Allah, exalted, had judged it in the Preserved Tablet, its occurrence was necessary and its omission impossible. Because we have shown that its omission would necessitate the turning of Allah's truthful news into falsehood, which is impossible. And as for what they mentioned in the second point, it is very weak. This is because distinguishing the messengers with those honors and those virtues does not necessitate the occurrence of enmity. Do you not see that those virtues are what became strong causes for the occurrence of intense love in the hearts of the saints? And if the occurrence of those virtues necessitated the occurrence of enmity, then one cause would necessitate the occurrence of two opposites, which is impossible. Rather, the truth is that that does not necessitate either the occurrence of love or the occurrence of enmity. And that which necessitates the occurrence of love is the casting of motives of love into hearts, and that which necessitates the occurrence of enmity is the casting of motives of enmity into hearts. On this basis, everything is from Allah. And when the issue of the motive (al-da'i) is recalled in the manner we summarized, it becomes apparent that the apparent meaning of His saying, exalted: 'And thus We made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals' is confirmed by this decisive rational proof, which no one is able to cast doubt upon in any way. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof and contains a lengthy dialectic. The author first cites two verses that explicitly say 'We made for every prophet an enemy.' The apparent meaning is that Allah creates enmity. Then an objection is raised: could the word 'ja'l' here mean 'judgment' (i.e., Allah merely judges them to be enemies) rather than creating? The author gives a preliminary response: the virtues bestowed on prophets naturally cause envy, so it is as if Allah made them enemies. Then the author provides supporting evidence from verses showing Allah supports prophets, implying He would not cast enmity into hearts—so the interpretation as judgment is needed. But then the author delivers the final answer: first, interpreting 'ja'l' as judgment is against the apparent meaning. Second, even if we accept that interpretation, if Allah's judgment is in the Preserved Tablet, then the occurrence of enmity becomes necessary (since Allah's news is true), so it still amounts to creation of enmity by necessity. Third, the alternative explanation that the virtues themselves cause enmity is weak because the same virtues cause love in saints, and one cause cannot produce two opposites. The true cause of enmity is the casting of motives into hearts, which is from Allah. Thus all is from Allah, and the verse is confirmed by rational proof. This is a classic kalam argument for the creation of all actions, even those of enemies.

Key Terms
اللوح المحفوظ
الداعي
الكرامات
الحسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that the virtues of prophets directly cause enmity in disbelievers, so Allah does not directly create the enmity.
Correction: The author shows that the same virtues cause love in saints, so one cause cannot produce two opposites. enmity must come directly from Allah through casting motives.

Checkpoint
What is the author's argument against the idea that the virtues of prophets cause enmity?
A) Virtues only cause love.
B) One cause cannot produce two opposite effects (love and enmity).
C) The virtues are not real.
D) The prophets do not have virtues.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof confirms that Allah creates enmity by casting motives into hearts, not through the virtues themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel enmity or dislike towards someone, do you examine your heart to see whether that feeling is from your own reasoning or from a motive that Allah has placed? How can you safeguard against attributing your negative feelings solely to external causes while ignoring Allah's role?
?
The prophets had the most virtuous qualities, yet some people still hated them. Consider a person in your life whom you find it hard to love. Could it be that your heart's hardness is a direct trial from Allah, and what would it take for you to ask Him to replace enmity with love?
?
If you truly believed that every motive of love or enmity in your heart is directly from Allah, how would that change the way you treat those who oppose you? Would you still hold grudges, or would you see them as part of Allah's decree and seek His help to change your own heart?

Seventh Proof: The Verse on Hardened Hearts
The seventh proof cites a Quranic verse on hardened hearts and refers back to the earlier discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse on hardened hearts serves as a seventh proof for the createdness of actions and how its discussion mirrors the previous proof.

Core Idea
The same objection and answer apply to both the sixth and seventh proofs.

The seventh proof is a concise application of the same rational argument used in the sixth proof, but now grounded in a clear Quranic verse. The verse states that Allah made the hearts hard, which implies direct creation. The author then explains that the entire dialectical discussion—question and answer—is identical to what preceded, meaning the same refutations and defenses apply.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice its brevity and explicit reference to the prior discussion.
This proof is the shortest in the sequence.
2
Identify the key term 'ja'l'
The verb 'ja'ala' (made) is central. Consider its theological implications: does it mean creation or something else?
The same term was debated in the sixth proof.
3
Understand the repetition
Why does the author repeat the same discussion? This shows that the rational argument is not dependent on a single verse but applies to all similar expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : قوله تعالى : ( وجعلنا قلوبهم قاسية (1) ) والكلام سؤالاً وجواباً : عين ما تقدم .
The seventh proof: His saying, exalted: 'And We made their hearts hard (1).' And the discussion, question and answer, is exactly the same as what preceded.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This is a brief proof. The author cites the verse in which Allah says 'We made their hearts hard.' The author then states that the entire discussion—including the same objection and answer that were given for the sixth proof—applies verbatim to this verse. This means the apparent meaning (that Allah creates hardness in hearts) is to be taken literally, and any attempts to reinterpret 'ja'l' as mere judgment or as resulting from other causes are refuted in the same way. This proof is thus a concise application of the previous rational argument.

A) It is an entirely new argument.
B) It is exactly the same discussion.
C) It is a weaker version.
D) It is only about punishment.

Key Takeaway
The seventh proof demonstrates that the same rational argument for creation of actions applies directly to the Quranic statement that Allah made hearts hard.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel your heart hardens towards obeying Allah, do you truly believe that Allah created that hardness? How does that belief change what you do next?
?
The verse states 'We made their hearts hard.' If Allah is the Creator of the hardness, then what blame do you have for your own hardness? Yet, you are still commanded to soften your heart. How do you reconcile these two realities in your daily struggle?
?
How does the fact that the same rational argument from the previous proof applies here confront your tendency to make excuses when your heart feels distant from Allah? What specific step will you take today to seek softness from Him?

The Eighth Proof: The Devil's Casting as a Trial
Eighth proof with objection and beginning of response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse about the devil's casting supports the Ash'ari position that Allah is the ultimate creator of all actions, including those attributed to the devil.

Core Idea
Allah makes the devil's casting a trial, proving His ultimate control over all events.

This lesson examines the eighth proof from the text, which uses the verse 'That He may make what the devil casts a trial.' The author addresses an objection that the verse attributes the casting to the devil, which might seem to contradict divine omnipotence. By clarifying that Allah's 'making' of the casting as a trial does not entail direct creation of the devil's whispers, the proof reinforces the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition (kasb).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage from the source. Notice how the author cites the verse and then presents an objection.
The text is incomplete, but focus on the structure: proof → objection → response.
2
Understand the objection
The objection claims the verse attributes the casting to the devil, which would support the view that humans create their own actions. Identify why this might be a problem for the Ash'ari position.
The opponent could argue that if the devil casts, then the devil creates that action, not Allah.
3
Analyze the author's response
The author argues that the verse emphasizes Allah's making (ja'l) of the casting as a trial, not the creation of the casting itself. 'Fitna' here means a distinguishing sign between believers and hypocrites.
The answer begins by addressing the attribution, but the text cuts off. Still, the key point is that Allah's role as the maker of the trial does not conflict with the devil's role as the caster.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
This proof shows that even acts attributed to the devil are ultimately under Allah's control, as He makes them serve a purpose. This aligns with the doctrine that Allah creates all actions, while humans acquire them.
Consider how this argument supports the Ash'ari view against the Qadariyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : قوله تعالى : ( ليجعل ما يلقى الشيطان فتنة (٢) ) فإن قيل : ظاهر هذا النص حجة عليكم . لأنه تعالى أضاف الإلقاء إلى الشيطان . ثم نقول : هذا النص يدل على أنه تعالى يجعل ما يلقيه الشيطان فتنة . والمراد من الفتنة : العلامة المميزة للذين في قلوبهم مرض ، عن الذين ما كانوا كذلك . يقال : فتنة . إذا امتحنته . ولا يلزم من قولنا : جعل ما يلقيه الشيطان علامة لبعض الأمور . قولنا : إنه تعالى هو الذي خلق تلك الوساوس الباطلة التي يلقيها الشيطان في القلوب
والجواب : قوله : إنه تعالى أضاف الإلقاء إلى الشيطان، إضافة الفعل
The eighth proof: His saying, exalted: 'That He may make what the devil casts a trial (2).' If it is said: The apparent meaning of this text is an argument against you, because He, exalted, attributed the casting to the devil. Then we say: This text indicates that He, exalted, makes what the devil casts a trial. And what is meant by 'trial' (fitna) is the distinguishing sign for those in whose hearts is a disease, from those who are not like that. It is said: fitan, if you test him. And it does not follow from our saying: 'He made what the devil casts a sign for some matters' that we say: He, exalted, is the one who created those false whisperings that the devil casts into hearts. And the answer: His saying that He, exalted, attributed the casting to the devil, attribution of the action...
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth proof and begins an objection-and-answer. The author cites the verse 'That He may make what the devil casts a trial.' An objection is raised: the verse attributes the casting to the devil, which seems to support the opponent's view that actions are not entirely created by Allah. The author responds by clarifying that 'make' (ja'l) refers to Allah making the devil's casting a means of trial or distinction between believers and hypocrites. The author then argues that saying Allah makes the devil's casting a sign does not entail that Allah creates the devil's whisperings themselves. However, the text breaks off at the beginning of the answer where the author presumably argues that the attribution of the casting to the devil does not negate divine creation of its substance or that it is an attribution of causation rather than creation. The incomplete nature of the text limits the full argument, but the clear thrust is that the verse actually supports the Ash'ari position that Allah is the ultimate creator of all actions, including those attributed to the devil, since the devil's casting is itself made a trial by Allah's act.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since the devil casts whispers, the whispers are entirely the devil's creation; the author argues that Allah makes them a trial, implying divine involvement.
Correction: The verse shows that Allah makes the devil's casting a trial, so the devil's actions are not independent but subservient to Allah's purpose.

Checkpoint

A) Punishment
B) Distinguishing sign
C) Misguidance

Key Takeaway
The verse 'That He may make what the devil casts a trial' actually supports the Ash'ari position because Allah's act of making the trial does not conflict with the devil's casting but subordinates it to divine purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Consider a sinful whisper that comes to your mind. Do you automatically blame the devil, or do you acknowledge that Allah has allowed it as a test for you? What does your response reveal about your belief in Allah's complete control?
?
If everything is from Allah, including the test, then your reaction to a trial is also part of the test. Are you ready to be held accountable for how you respond to the whisperings and trials that come your way? What change will you make today to ensure your heart remains sound?

Ninth Proof: God Making Imams of Guidance and Misguidance
The author presents the verse about imams and responds to an objection questioning the benefit of such making.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ninth proof based on God making imams of guidance and misguidance, the objection that this is futile under determinism, and the beginning of the author's response through two interpretations.

Core Idea
The Quranic imams pose a problem for determinism that the author answers with judgment/naming and eschatological roles.

This lesson examines a theological proof from the Quran about God making imams of guidance and imams calling to the Fire. The author presents an objection that such making would be meaningless under a deterministic view. He then begins his response by offering two interpretations: one labeling it a matter of divine judgment and naming, and another relating it to the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof from the verses
Read the two Quranic verses about God making imams of guidance and imams calling to the Fire. Notice the author's explanation that 'making' means creating the attribute in them.
The verses are a proof for the author's position.
2
Understand the objection
The objection argues that if God creates faith and disbelief, then appointing imams is futile. Consider the two cases: calling a believer (futile) and calling a disbeliever (impossible).
This objection challenges the apparent meaning of the verses under jabr.
3
Note the author's initial response
The author states that such making must have an interpretation. This sets up his reply that the verses are not to be taken literally.
4
Examine the two interpretations given
The author lists two interpretations: first, it could be a matter of judgment and naming (i.e., God declaring them imams in His decree), and second, it could refer to the Hereafter where they call followers to the Fire. The passage ends mid-sentence.
The answer is incomplete; the full response may continue on the next page.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : قوله تعالى : ( وجعلناهم أئمة يهدون بأمرنا (۱) ) وقوله : ( وجعلناهم أئمة يدعون إلى النار (۲) ) وجعل الشيء : شيئاً آخر عبارة : عن تحصيل تلك الصفة فيه . يقال : فلان جعل هذا الثوب أسود ، أو أبيض . أي حصل فيه صفة السواد وصفة البياض ، فكذا ههنا . المراد من جعلهم أئمة الهدى، وأئمة النار : خلق صفة الهدى وصفة الضلال فيهم فإن قيل : هذه الآية لا يمكن إجراؤها على ظاهرها ، لأنه لو كان خالق الإيمان والكفر هو الله تعالى ، لم يكن لجعل هذا إماماً في الهدى ، وجعل ذاك إماما في الضلال معنى. لأن إمام الهدى، إن دعى المؤمن إلى الهدى فهو عبث . لأن الله تعالى ، لما خلق الهدى في المؤمن ، كانت دعوته إلى الهدى عبثاً . وإن دعي الكافر إلى الهدى فهو محال . لأن من خلق الله الكفر فيه ، امتنع صيرورته مؤمناً . وكذا القول في الإمام الداعي إلى النار . فإنه لا يخلو من هذين الوجهين . فثبت : أن على مذهب الجبر لا يبقى في جعل الشخص إماماً في الهدى ، وإماماً في الضلال فائدة . وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لا بد لهذا الجعل من تأويل . وهو أحد أمرين : أحدهما : الحكم والتسمية. والثاني : أن يحمل ذلك على أحوال القيامة . وذلك لأنهم في الآخرة يدعون أصحابهم إلى النار . كما قال في حق فرعون : ( يقدم قومه يوم القيامة . فأوردهم النار (۳) ) ومما يقوي ذلك :
The ninth proof: His statement, the Exalted: (And We made them imams guiding by Our command) and His statement: (And We made them imams calling to the Fire). And making something another thing is an expression for acquiring that attribute in it. It is said: So-and-so made this garment black or white, meaning he acquired in it the attribute of blackness and the attribute of whiteness. So likewise here. The meaning of making them imams of guidance and imams of the Fire is: creating the attribute of guidance and the attribute of misguidance in them. If it is said: This verse cannot be applied according to its apparent meaning, because if the Creator of faith and disbelief is God, then there would be no meaning in making this one an imam in guidance and that one an imam in misguidance. Because the imam of guidance, if he calls a believer to guidance, it is futile, since God created guidance in the believer, so his call to guidance is futile. And if he calls a disbeliever to guidance, it is impossible, because whoever God created disbelief in cannot become a believer. Likewise the imam calling to the Fire: it is not free from these two aspects. So it is established that on the doctrine of jabr (determinism) there remains no benefit in making a person an imam in guidance and an imam in misguidance. And when this is established, we say: This making must have an interpretation. It is one of two things: The first: judgment and naming. The second: that it be carried to the conditions of the Resurrection, because in the Hereafter they call their followers to the Fire, as He said concerning Pharaoh: (He will precede his people on the Day of Resurrection and lead them into the Fire). And what strengthens that is:
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth proof from two Quranic verses about God making imams (leaders) of guidance and imams calling to the Fire. The author first explains that 'making' here means creating the attribute in them. Then an objection is raised: if God creates both faith and disbelief, then appointing imams is pointless. The imam of guidance either calls a believer (futile) or a disbeliever (impossible because God created disbelief in him). Similarly for the imam of misguidance. This objection argues that determinism (jabr) renders the appointment of imams meaningless. The author then begins his response by stating that such a making must have an interpretation, and he lists two possibilities: first, it could be a matter of judgment and naming (i.e., God judges them to be such in His decree), and second, it could refer to the Hereafter where imams call their followers to the Fire. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'And what strengthens that is...' indicating the answer is incomplete. This lesson covers the objection and the start of the author's answer.

Key Terms

أئمة الهدى
أئمة النار
الجبر
تأويل
الحكم والتسمية
أحوال القيامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection represents the author's own belief.
Correction: The objection is a hypothetical argument from a determinist perspective that the author then refutes.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why is it meaningless to make an imam of guidance under determinism?
A) Because the imam might lead people astray
B) Because calling a believer to guidance is futile and calling a disbeliever is impossible
C) Because God does not create faith
D) Because humans have free will

Key Takeaway
The ninth proof shows that determinists cannot explain why God would make imams; the author counters with interpretations that preserve divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you struggle to guide someone to truth, do you ever secretly feel it's futile because Allah has already decreed their state? How does the ninth proof challenge that feeling and what one thing will you do differently in your next interaction?
?
If you knew that your calling someone to good could be the very means by which Allah creates guidance in them, would you be more persistent or more lazy? What is holding you back from taking that risk?
?
Think of someone you consider an 'imam of misguidance' in your community. Do you see them as a test for your own faith or as an excuse to abandon da'wah? How does the author's emphasis on Allah's wisdom in making such imams change your duty towards them?
